text:
I took the repeated suggestions of other reviewers and added 2 T. of vegetable oil and 1 tsp. vanilla. For more intense "chocolatiness" I also added 1 tsp. of chocolate extract. I don't know if these additions and changes were necessary, but I do know this was one fantastic cookie! Everything was just perfect--it's an attractive cookie, perfectly shaped (I used a small ice cream scoop), kind of almost pebbly on the top. The texture was also perfect-- a little crackly, chewey on the outside, and melt-in-your mouth soft on the inside. Instead of chocolate chips I used chopped Andes mints, and the taste combination was out of this world, with no hint of cake mix taste. The flavor variations with this recipe are, of course, endless, but I enjoyed this combination so much I don't know that I'll bother trying it any other way. I do know, however, that I won't be making this with a yellow cake mix as the cake mix taste is hard to cover up. I also know this is only the first of many times I will come back to this easy and delicious recipe.

text:
Oh man, this is the BEST basic cake-mix cookie recipe.  I love strawberry cake, so that was the mix I used and added 1 cup white chips and 1 cup pecans and it made the most yummy cookies.  I used a 2 tsp. scoop and made 44 2-inch cookies.  I've noticed with this and other cake mix cookie recipies that the cookies do not spread while baking, so unless you want puffy round drops, you need to flatten the cookies out a bit before you put them in the oven.

text:
WOW WOW WOW!  I've been a baker all my life and wanted to find an easy cookie recipe to make with my 4 yr. daughter and this one takes the cake.  I've tried 3 other cake mix cookies from this site, and this is by far #1.  You can use any kind of cake mix, I like Butter Yellow because is gives a nice buttery taste and I took another reviewer's advice and added 2 tablespoon oil.  This keeps the cookie SUPER moist.  Definitely an 8 min. cookie if you want moist & chewy and stays this way for days--if it last that long in your house.  Great to make with kids, many variations possible and good for giving or when you're in a pinch.  Look no further for the 'short-cut' cookie recipe!!  I love these! (and so does my waistline)- Aahh!

text:
My grandma taught me how to make theses when I was little. You can use any flavor cake mix along with 2 eggs and 1/2 cup oil instead of butter. You practically can't mess these up! I love to use butter pecan cake mixes or red velvet with cream cheese frosting! My husband likes a spice cake mix with a packet instant oatmeal, 1/2 cup brown sugar and 1 cup riasins. They seem to stay soft even without being sealed extra tight. My best advice, don't overbake them and you'll never go wrong. A great thing to experiment with, get the kid's involved!

text:
HELPFUL TIP FOR THICK AND CHEWY: I was worried about mine turning out flat like many users said but I think the problem is they are overmixing.  Use room temp butter, and as the directions say "STIR" with spoon not mixer.  After you've "smushed" in the butter into the batter, and the must add 2T oil, and 1t vanilla, THEN add the eggs and chocolate chips.  I also then stick this in the fridge for 30 min or even overnight when I'm preparing ahead ...or in the freezer for 15 min.  I bake for 10 min (my oven is quick).  Basically if you let this cool on the cookie sheet for 15 min. and the middle is still too gooey, just stick it in the oven again, and add 4 min.  I do this with any cookie recipe, and always works.  I posted 2 pics.  One after not putting in fridge BUT NOT OVERMIXING, and then ones left in fridge plus NOT OVERMIXING.  Clearly a difference in thickness.  My husband likes flat and chewy, and I like thick and chewy, so both work! You can use yellow cake mix w/1/2C oats and 1/2C chocolate chips.  Yum! A wonderful fast recipe with many ways to experiment!

text:
Great moist cookie if you like soft & chewy.  I used Duncan Hines Moist Deluxe, Devil's Food Cake Mix and replaced chocolate chips with peanut butter chips.  I added no oil-just the 1 stick butter and 2 eggs - like the recipe says.  I spooned the batter out on the cookie sheets and baked at 350F for 10 minutes.  The dough spread out easily but didn't totally flatten, nor burn on the bottom.  These came out perfectly for me.  I just made cookies again this time using Pillsbury Moist Surpreme (with the pudding in the mix), Golden Butter Recipe.  I used 1 stick of butter and 2 eggs, but I also added 1 tsp. of vanilla, 1/2 cup finely chopped walnuts and 1 cup choc chips.   I did not add any extra oil.  I dropped by tablespoon and baked for 12 minutes at 350F.  Again I got a nice, spread cookie ~2 inches in diameter with a golden-brown bottom.  I don't think the extra oil is needed for the pudding-type or extra moist cake mixes.

text:
So many reviewers said to add 2 tablespoons of oil plus a teaspoon of vanilla extract, so that was what I did.  I like to bake most of my desserts from scratch so I felt a bit like I was cheating by using a boxed cake mix... but the cookies turned out SO GOOD -- soft and chewy!  I've tried many good from-scratch cookie recipes but they're never this soft and chewy.  I know many friends are going to ask for the recipe once they try these cookies and I'm going to have to sheepishly say it's actually a boxed cake mix!  Anyway, I was able to get 25 3-inch cookies and they spread to just the right thickness on their own -- I didn't have to flatten them a bit before baking like some reviewers had to.  I added walnuts along w/ milk chocolate chips and they were picture-perfect.  I baked at 350 F for 10 minutes and at first, they looked as if they might be a little under-baked or too gooey, but after they cooled completely, they were perfect.  Put them in an airtight container and they were still super soft and chewy the next morning (didn't harden up).

text:
This is an amazing cookie! Super moist and gooey inside and slightly crispy & chewy on the outside. I used a 9oz box of devils food cake mix to yield 16 large cookies. (I can't make more than that.. I would eat them all in 1 night!) Here are the subs I made to get the calorie per cookie to 100: 9oz devils food cake mix, 1/3C Light I Can't Believe its Not Butter, 24g pureed prune (3-4 prunes, reconstituted in a little hot water, blended) 3Tbs semi sweet choc chips & 1 bar (34g) sugar free dark chocolate, coarsely chopped. Used 1 egg and added 1/2 tsp vanilla extract. I baked them 10 minutes on parchment paper (they still looked underdone) but after resting them 2 minutes on the sheet & 2 minutes still on the paper on a wire rack, they were perfect! Perfectly spread, crackled tops and slightly gooey inside even after a day. They are so decadent and chocolately and wonderful with a glass of pinot noir at dessert time. My friends can't believe they're made with prunes and cake mix or that they're low cal and more heart healthy than your average cookie. I love this recipe... thanks for the inspiration :)

text:
This is a good start to your basic cake mix cookie recipe, but I made the following changes:
1 egg, plus 1 egg yolk
1 tsp pure vanilla extract

I always beat the softened butter together with the dry cake mix until crumbly (any cake mix will work---even store-brand) and add the eggs until combined. I then add the vanilla and fold in chocolate chunks/chips etc. 

Using a 2 TBSP cookie scoop, I place them 2" apart on a parchment lined cookie sheet and bake for 12 min @ 350F.  These will spread, and result in a cookie that has a crispy outer shell and chewy inside. 

These are my go-to cookies for bake sales as they are quick, easy and inexpensive, especially when making 20 dozen.

And not being a big fan of cake mix cookies, I never thought to try chocolate cake mix instead of regular chocolate cookie batter. I bought several boxes of Betty Crocker cake mix on sale, so that's what I used. Then after reading some other reviews, I made sure to add 2 Tbsp vegetable oil and 1 tsp vanilla. I also substituted the baking Andes mints for reg chocolate chips. I used my small pampered chef cookie scooper to make the balls. 9 minutes was the magic time for these cookie in the oven. My first couple pans experienced quite a bit of speading because the batter had become warm, but after putting it in the fridge for a little bit they came out wonderful. Very easy to make, got lots of compliments. You couldn't even taste the cakey flavor. They remained soft and chewy for days (I made mine 3 days ago). A friend said using butter yellow cake mix with butterscotch chips and adding a little cinnamon makes a good combo as well. I am so happy I've finally found a good chocolate cookie recipe!!

text:
Oh, my goodness!  This just became my favorite cookie, and I have been making all sorts of cookies for years!  So easy to make, but so moist and chocolatey...  I omitted the 1 cup of chocolate chips because I used a triple chocolate fudge cake mix with chocolate chips already in it.  Instead of butter, I used margarine because that was what I had on hand.  I followed other reviewers' recommendations and added 2 tablespoons of canola oil and 1 teaspoon of vanilla extract.  The dough was still so thick that my hand mixer could not handle it.  I ended up using a wooden spoon to finish the mixing.  I scooped the dough by leveled tablespoonfuls, and the batch yieled about 40 cookies.  My baking time was about 11 minutes.  I will definitely make these cookies again in a few days for Christmas!

text:
OK, I have to admit, the first time I made these, they turned out horrible! The package of cake mix that I used was only 16 oz., so the proportions were off, and then I left them in the oven for too long, so they got really hard. I was ready to throw away this recipe, but I decided to give it another try. I used a different cake mix (Dr. Oetker's organic chocolate cake mix), and I substituted coconut oil for some of the butter. (Coconut oil is VERY good for you, and it's also great for baking!) I threw in a mixture of bittersweet chocolate chips and white chocolate chips, as well as 1-2 tsp. of peppermint extract. I baked them for exactly 8 minutes, and they came out perfect. They taste just like thin mints! Oh, and I got a whopping 50 cookies out of this batch!

I made this with Betty Crocker chocolate cake mix, 1/4 cup white chocolate chips, 1/2 cup chopped up Palmers peppermint bark and 1/2 cup semi sweet chips. I really liked how they turned out especially the white chocolate against the dark brown. Soft and flat and chewy! Yum!

text:
Basically, I made 4 batches.  The first was with a brownie mix due to my error - don't use they will be flat.  I read the reviews and took their word at adding the 2T of oil and 1t of vanilla. I will also add to make sure to use butter and not margarine. After my brownie fiasco,(they were delicious just not presentable) I made the cookies using Betty Crocker Yellow Super Moist cake mix.  I mixed everything (by hand)except the oil and chips. I added Heath toffee bits.  The cookies turned out nice and made about 40 cookies. I actually rolled them in a ball and they turned out fine. The next batch I used a store brand white mix. I mixed the oil in with everything else, just to see if it made a difference. It didn't seem to.  I used butterscotch chips with those, but for some reason it took longer to bake these cookies. Those also made 40.The last batch I used Better Crocker super moist white with no egg yokes and margarine (country crock light).  It turned out more creamy and less dough like. I let it sit a bit to stiffen up. It helped. They came out just fine and made 36. Great, fast recipe.

text:
4 stars for the few ingredients and quick prep time. They tasted good for a quick substitute. I did as others suggested and added an additional 2 tbsp oil and 1 tsp vanilla extract. I used BC triple Choc cake mix, 1/2 C Choc chips and 1/3 C + 4 tbsp chopped maraschino cherries. Next time i'll do devils food. The triple Choc was way too much. And this coming from a pregnant person craving Choc. I baked on parchment paper. I varied the batter size scoops. Using ~1+1/2 tbsp of batter and placing in mounds size of 50 cent pieces they took 11-12 mins @ 350. 2 tsp size scoops plopped in mounds took 9 mins@  350'F. They do flatten and spread out. I let them cool completely, for 5 mins, and removed immediately off parchment w/ no issues. BUT do not stack them. They will stick together b/c they are a mix between cookie and cake like. So separate w/ foil or parchment when stacking. The size of your cookie (or any food for that matter) will alter baking/cooking time. Smaller= shorter and bigger vol=longer. Also, if using convection in the oven, the fan circulates the hot air, so the temp needs to be dropped around 325'F possibly. I worked in a bakery for 8 yrs and they use convection. Since the cookies were super chocolatey I made some into ice cream sandwiches w/ vanilla ice cream and some I used a light cherry flavored frosting. Since it's so hot the ice cream one's were much more appealing. Thanks for sharing a good/quick recipe.

I make cake mix cookies all the time.  To avoid the cake mix taste, add a few drops of mint extract to chocolate cake mix, or a few drops of lemon extract to yellow cake mix.  For most cake mixes, 1/3 cup of oil is enough, or use orange juice (1/2 and 1/2) with oil.  I always have people ask me for my recipe when I serve cake mix cookies!

text:
What an easy cookie mix!!  I love how you can tweak this with different cake mix varieties and add-ins.  I made batch using devil's food cake mix, 1/2 cup of apple sauce, 2 eggs, and a LOT of chocolate chips.  I made a second batch using a spice cake mix, 1/2 cup apple sauce, 2 eggs, 1/2 cup raisins, and 1/2 cup of white chocolate chips.  Both turned out GREAT!!  They don't spread out much, so if you don't want thick cookies, you should let the batter warm up a bit or press them down when you put the dough on the cookie sheet.  I got great reviews from my family & friends for both cookies.  I also think these cookies (the chocolate version) would make great "whoopie pie" cookies!

text:
This is the recipe you need for that last minute bake sale that you just found out about! This cookie is as close to the best in brownie as you can get! Firm enough to pick up but melt in your mouth moist and gooey tender. Chocolate perfection. I added about a teaspoon of vanilla to the recipe. I cooked them at 350 for 9 minutes because I have a hot oven. Just ccok them until they are set not brown. 1 minute to many will make a huge difference. Let them cool. There was no cake mix taste at all! This is a great secret emergency recipe for bake sales, class room parties,potlucks, guest coming over with short notice, new neighbors and hungry after school children. The hungry children can even be taught to make it themselves in minutes. With an 88 cent mix and 1/2 hour you have lots of fantiasic "homemade" cookies. I even wipped up a second batch while the first was cooking without difficulty.

This concept makes the best cookies. I use yellow cake mix and TONS of chocolate chips.The secret to big thick cookies is to chill the dough for 30 mins before baking. I then bake them until just set and let them cool. The result is a thick, soft, moist amazing cookie.

text:
Like many that came before me... I also added 2T oil and some vanilla.

The best thing about this recipe is it's versatility.

I made my cookies from a spice cake mix.  I added mini chocolate chips, walnuts and raisins.  I also punched it up with some pumpkin pie spice.

They are easy!

Some pointers that others have mentioned:  The dough is very stiff, a hand mixer will likely not be able to handle it.  My stand KA had no problem.

The chocolate versions are a bit sweet.  A lot depends on your mix choice.

It is a little cake-ier than many cookies... I have no problem with this, but if you do, change the recipe to one egg and one egg yolk.

text:
This gets a 5 for ease of preparation and modifiability (lol). I used yellow cake mix (regular 515g box) and added 1 tsp. vanilla extract. Divided the dough in two. In the first half, I added about 3/4 c. toffee bits. Yummy and not overly sweet! The dough is very sticky, though, so it is easiest to work with it chilled. It did spread and the top crackled nicely. In the 2nd half, I stirred in 3/4 c. peanut butter, rolled into balls, and pressed down with a fork. This dough was much less sticky and easy to work with. Bakes to almost 2x its size & makes yummy peanut butter cookies. So easy! NOTE: wait for cookies to completely cool before removing from cookie sheet, otherwise you'll leave behind bits of cookie. *** I have to update this review because the toffee bit variation is the best damned cookie I've had in a long time. I flatten it and it turns into a sweet crispy deliciousness. Everyone loves it.

text:
VERY PEDESTRIAN COOKIE. I knew this going in but I was looking for something easy and fast that tasted pretty good. I never expected to knock this out of the park but I wasn't expecting a flop either. This was a flop.  I took the advice of another reviewer and added 2 tablespoons oil and some vanilla. I didn't have chocolate extract on hand and I wish I had -- these needed it despite using a Duncin Heinz rich chocolate fudge cake mix. I make my cakes from scratch now so I can barely tolerate the mix stuff anymore and this is why -- they lack flavor. I knew better and am kicking myself for even trying it. I also added almost a full box of Andes mints like the first reviewer did but they need at least two boxes. I think the chocolate chips would have been better because they might have improved slightly on the chocolate flavor this so desperately lacks. My oven is powerful and I should not have baked these at 350. They flattened out and got crispy that way and I used two eggs and some oil plus buter so that should NOT have happened. The second batch I baked at 330 and had to take them out half raw to avoid them getting crispy on me.  Don't waste your time with this when there are so many other good cookie recipes out there. What was I thinking?!!!!!!!!

Fan-Freakin-Tastic!  I followed other's advice...1/2 c oil, 1 egg, cake mix, 2 tbsp water, 1 cup of mint choc chips into Betty Crocker Triple Choc Fudge cake mix. Baked at 350 for 9 minutes. The cookies turned out thick and chunky looking with the right amount of crunch on the outside and little bit soft on the inside.  I don't care for chewy cookies so these were perfect. One of the cookies didn't get any mint chips and I tasted it "plain"...the taste was a little dull as other's have reviewed.  These cookies are best with something incorporated into the batter...nuts, pb chips...something. This is how I will make cookies from now on.  Love this!

text:
WOW!! I loved this recipe!!! I followed others advice and added 2T of oil and 1t of vanilla to the recipe and it was great!! It make 30 cookies and I baked both sheets at once. I left the racks to close to each other so, the top sheet looked "cracked" (like others said) but the bottom sheet looked too moist so, I turned the oven off and left it in there for 3 mins. It still didn't come out looking "cracked" but I could tell they were done. Oh man the difference was delicious. The 8 min "cracked" cookies were gooey but the cookies that stayed in the warm oven for 3 extra minutes were perfect. I honestly can't believe how good they came out. Not cake like at all and they spread quite a bit. I really don't like baking cookies but I have to admit that hubby will go nuts for these and because it's such an easy recipe, I'll be making them ALOT this holiday!

text:
These are the least expensive, fastest, easiest, tastiest cookies to make. Thanks to other reviewers, I tweaked the recipe a little and now think of them as "One Cookies"...One chocolate cake mix, one stick of melted butter, one egg, one tsp. of vanilla, one handful of chocolate chips. So easy to clean up...One mixing bowl, one cereal bowl (for melting the butter), and one spoon. I was done mixing before the oven was done pre-heating. And there is no need to drag out the electric mixer. My new oven is very accurate (yay!) and they bake at 350 for 9 minutes.

text:
I didn't really know how to rate the original recipe, since I strayed so far from it!  Made these using a Duncan Hines Devil's Food cake mix.  Added the Reviewers' recommended 2 T. oil and 1 t. vanilla.  Also added a pinch of salt and about 1 t. instant coffee granules mixed with a few drops of water.  (These are difficult to mix - make sure your butter is room temp - my arm was sore from mixing!)  Cut dough into thirds and made 3 different kinds.  Craisins, white choc. chips and walnuts; Skor candy bar; Reese's Peanut Butter cups.  I baked them all for somewhere between 13 and 15 minutes.  The craisin cookies were quite soft after cooling.  The Reese's and Skor cookies were more firm, but still soft after being completely cooled.   I ended up putting all back into the oven on 200 for about 15 minutes.  Now I have pretty crisp cookies!  This was quite a bit of work, but they taste pretty good with the add-ins and now I know what to do.  Don't skimp on the add-ins!  *****Also wanted to mention that these puff up quite a bit while baking, but start to flatten as soon as they come out of the oven.  I used a small cookie scoop which worked nicely and didn't flatten them at all - they spread out on their own while baking.  Perhaps adding a little flour would them stay a little puffed-up?  Also, not a strong choc. flavor, but could add cocoa or choc. chips.  I posted a pic.  Made about 33 cookies.

text:
WOW. This cookie was extremely delicious! Instead of the chocolate cake mix and chocolate chips I used carrot cake mix with white chocolate chips and they were insanely good.  I found that the batter was a bit thick and the chips didn't really adhere well to the batter nicely, so I added some vegetable oil and everything turned out fine. My first 2 batches were without the vegetable oil and my last batch and a half was with the oil, and they both turned out excellent. I also purchased sqeezable cream cheese frosting that comes in a whipped cream spray type bottle, so people can just put on frosting as they desired. The cookie tastes perfectly fine without the frosting, but either way is delicious.  I ate about 6 of these cookies in one night and my dad ended up eating about 12! Needless to say, they didn't last very long and were so rich and delicious!

text:
First i must say i am an old fashion make from scratch dessert person and was very skeptical but these really impressed me, they were really easy and very tasty. These were soo easy and very good. *HINT* melt the butter completely, so there is more liquid to mix the batter, i made three batches, 1 with milk chocolate cake and 1 cup semi sweet chips, 1 with butter pecan added 1/2 cup chopped pecans and topped the cookie with a pecan half, and 1 with strawberry cake and mixed in 3/4 cup white chocolate chips. I would recommend 1/2 -3/4 cup of either chocolate chips or white chips, i felt 1 cup was too much. The strawberry cake makes a pretty pink cookie which little girls love! I think this is easily adaptable to any cake mix! All three batches made exactly 24 cookies. Darker pans take a minute or two less time.

We cleaned out the pantry yesterday and found two boxes of german chocolate cake mix that go bad in a couple weeks. My family asked me to find something to do with them so i decided to try these. They're not the most amazing baking feat i've ever made, but they are pretty darn good. I used a cup of pecans, since i'm out of chips, and they came out realy nice. They're soft and moist on the inside ((not undercooked)) and crispy along the edges.

Thanks so much for sharing! They're going on my holiday cookie sharing list.

I just finished baking these, and I am very impressed! I love how moist they turned out and I can't wait to make them again. So, I'm guessing the way to go is somewhere in between to get the right size and shape of the cookie.

text:
I used 1 whole egg and 1 egg yolk, rather than two eggs, then eventually just kneaded this with my hands to mix well.  I thought it was far too dry and didn't want dry cookies, so I took previous reviewers' advice and added some oil.  I didn't measure, I just added a little at a time until the batter seemed moist enough.  Also added about 1 tsp of vanilla.  I did press the dough down just a little, not much, and 8 minutes precisely did the trick.  You must let them cool on the pan, give them time to set.  Quite a delicious, simply treat.  They're soft and rich, just as expected.

I am VERY impressed by the outcome of these easy cookies!

A few modifications:
1. Used Reduced Sugar pillsbury cake mix.
2. Used extra 2 T Smart Balance oil per previous recommendations.
3. Used 1/2 c Smart Balance oil instead of butter as I was out!
4. Used M&Ms...do NOT add a cup of M&Ms as they do not hold onto the dough as well as would chocolate chips.

I will be making these OFTEN as they are DELICIOUS.  Thank you for the recipe!

text:
Wow, are these good!  I used a Devil's Food cake mix and followed the recipe directions.  Then I also added 2 tbsp. of oil, 1 tsp. vanilla and a partial bag of chocolate chips.  Used a cookie scoop and baked the cookies for 10 min.  When they came out, I let them sit on the sheet for 5 full minutes before moving them to a cooling rack.  They taste like moist, chewy brownies!  Definitely the easiest cookies I've ever made.

Update:  I made these a second time and used a Red Velvet cake mix, a bag of White Chocolate Peppermint M & M's and a leftover partial bag of mini chocolate chips.  I still added the oil and vanilla and baked for 10 minutes - they were wonderful and very festive looking.  I also realized how important it is to leave the cookies on the cookie sheet for a full 5 minutes after taking them out of the oven and before transferring them to a cooling rack.  Do not get anxious and skip this step!

text:
This is the second time I made these cookies. The first time I followed the recipe exactly. The cookies were good but came out puffy and tasted more like a brownie. This time I used Duncan Hines Dark Chocolate cake mix and as 1 reviewer suggested only one and half eggs. Since I was short on butter I used 1/4c of butter and 1/4c of lard. I creamed the butter and lard together and then added the egg, mixed thoroughly and then added in the cake mix and chocolate chips. The batter was fairly stiff and had to finish mixing with my hand to get everything incorporated.  I dropped by spoonful on a heavy baking sheet and baked for 9 minutes. The cookies came out perfect! Crispy on the edges and soft and chewy in the center. They are really the best and super easy to make and easy on the budget!

city:

region:

country:
None
text:
This recipe makes great cookies!!

I tried to reduce the butter, but as I was mixing it it seemed too dry, so I ended up keeping it at a full stick. Adding the 2T oil & 1t vanilla seemed to be an important addition to this recipe, because they turned out great this way.  One reviewer said to reduce the recipe by one egg white, but I used 2 large eggs and my cookies both held together well and were soft and chewy.  I do agree with the reviewer who said to flatten out your dough balls just a bit, and if possible refrigerate your dough balls a little bit before baking. I did one batch room temp and another 15 minutes of refrigeration after forming teaspoon balls, and they both turned out great but the refrigerated dough cookies were a bit prettier -- more perfectly round. 

I used Immaculate brand all-natural chocolate cake mix, Kerrygold grass-fed unsalted butter, organic Canola oil, and Trader Joes bourbon-based vanilla.  I topped my cookies with chopped walnuts, which for this recipe I think topping the cookies will work better than mix-ins. 

Really great cookies. I'm going to keep this on my short list.

They are amazing! Fluffy and a hit with the cookie monster... 
I did make a few changes. I added 1 TBSP vanilla, 1 TBSP veg. oil. And a dash of 1% milk. The batter was too thick otherwise. 
I used a Dunkin Hines pink cake mix. And with the chocolate chips they would be amazing for Valentines Day. 
I saw some reviews that they were too much like a cake. And well, it's a cake mix and cookie recipe.... It's gonna be fluffy and airy like a moist cake. If you're expecting a crumbly cookie, this isn't it.

text:
I took the suggestions of others and added 2 T of vegetable oil and 1 tsp vanilla.  Also, I melted the butter rather than just softened it (made stirring it up by hand easier).  I used a white cake mix and added milk chocolate chips and they were DELICIOUS!  I have also used chocolate cake mix with white chocolate chips - equally good! The most important thing is to not over cook them. I found in my oven that 8 minutes and 10 seconds is the perfect amount of time. Any more and they aren't as chewy-gooey and good... Every oven is different so keep a close eye!

text:
I make this recipe all the time with different cake mix flavors.  Instead of using butter, I use 1/3 cup of canola oil.  I bake for 6 minutes then start checking (You don't want these to overcook.) Mine are usually ready at 8 minutes. Let them cool on the cookie sheet ( I use a silpat) -they will continue to cook a little bit this way. Combo's that work for me:  Yellow cake w/choc. chips, chocolate cake w/walnuts or white choc chips, cherry chip cake is a winner with no additions, or funfetti with no additions.  Try a spice cake with raisins and instant oats for an oatmeal raisin cookie.  Everyone who tries these loves them!

I have made these before but today when I needed to make these in a pinch (a group my daughter's friends came over) I had to improvise a bit.  I only had one egg!  So I used the 1/2 c butter, one egg and then used 1/4c (just slightly more) of applesauce. I didn't even have apple sauce around, but I DID have apples.... so I sliced 2 apples,sprinkled with a bit of sugar and cinnamon and cooked in the microwave for a few minutes.  I mashed those, added to the rest of the ingredients and viola... I had great cookies for the kids!  I love this recipe cuz it is so easy!  (and **usually** have the ingredients around to make at any time!

I took the advice of others and added a little extra oil and vanilla and they turned out nice and soft.  Will use again!

text:
What an easy and versatile recipe, not to mention inexpensive.  This holiday season, I've made spice cookies with craisins and walnuts, chocolate with mint & dark chocolate chips, white with red and green m&m's, red velvet with white chocolate chips, and my favorite - yellow with chocolate chips.  They're so moist and delicious, that I'm having trouble keeping enough around to give to others - we keep devouring them!

** A tip - before handling the dough, spray your hands with cooking spray - this way, the dough won't stick to your hands.  You'll have to reapply the spray quite often though, because this dough is very sticky!

They said these were the best cookies they ever had.  *I also use this cake mix to make the Self-Filled cupcake recipe that you'll find here on All Recipes.  Those are always a big hit too!

text:
i thought these were great... i did only use one egg both times i've used this recipe to avoid the cookies being too cake like as some other reviewers have mentioned (and i dont think its neccessary to add any oil or vanilla flavoring to add moisture... if you mix the ingredients with your hands it has the perfect consisitancy, not too dry and moist enough to be just a TINY bit sticky, and wont make your cookies flatten out so much when you put them in the oven). the first time i made this i used a betty crocker triple chocolate fudge cake mix that already had mini chocolate chips added in the box. the second time i used a betty crocker lemon cake mix and didnt add any chips or anything to the mix. both times i shaped the mix into balls (about 1 inch thick) with my hands and rolled them in sugar before baking which make 50 cookies per box. i also used a dark non-stick pan (sprayed with pam!), so i baked my cookies at 325 degrees for 10 minutes. both times the cookies came out wonderful. this recipe is so easy, and the cookies come out very tasty! i'll be using this recipe several times over again w/ all sorts of cake mixes, thank you!

This recipe is a pretty good starting place.  I was just looking for something quick to throw together at the last minute to take to a church potluck, and this fit the bill. country:

text:
I really enjoyed this recipe, it was very easy and I love anything that comes out well with minimal effort. I would suggest that you be careful what kind of cake mix you use, because some of them have a more salty taste because they're supposed to "taste like butter" or have a dark chocolate flavor. If you taste your mix and it's a little salty, I would recommend either more brown sugar as suggested in the recipe, or using more chips (I definitely would not recommend cutting the amount of chips). I used a dark chocolate mix that was a little salty, so I used white chocolate to boost the sweet flavor and they came out very well. I also moved my baking rack up one to prevent the bottoms from burning. My cookies were crunchy when they came out of the oven. I was fine with that, but I stored them in a plastic container overnight and now they're soft and chewy.
